The Visit method is\n   337→// invoked for each node with the path leading to the node provided additionally.\n   338→// If the result visitor w is not nil and no error, Walk visits each of the children\n   339→// of node with the visitor w, followed by a call of w.Visit(nil, nil).\n   340→type Visitor interface {\n   341→\tVisit(node Node, path []Node) (w Visitor, err error)\n   342→}\n   343→\n   344→// Walk traverses an AST in depth-first order: It starts by calling\n   345→// v.Visit(node, path); node must not be nil. If the visitor w returned by\n   346→// v.Visit(node, path) is not nil and the visitor returns no error, Walk is\n   347→// invoked recursively with visitor w for each of the non-nil children of node,\n   348→// followed by a call of w.Visit(nil), returning an error\n   349→// As the tree is descended the path of previous nodes is provided.\n   350→func Walk(v Visitor, node Node, path []Node) error {\n   351→\tvar err error\n   352→\tif v, err = v.Visit(node, path); v == nil || err != nil {\n   353→\t\treturn err\n   354→\t}\n   355→\tvar pathToHere []Node // Initialized only when needed.\n   356→\n   357→\tfor e := range ChildrenIter(node) {\n   358→\t\tif pathToHere == nil {\n   359→\t\t\tpathToHere = append(path, node)\n   360→\t\t}\n   361→\t\tif err := Walk(v, e, pathToHere); err != nil {\n   362→\t\t\treturn err\n   363→\t\t}\n   364→\t}\n   365→\n   366→\t_, err = v.Visit(nil, nil)\n   367→\treturn err\n   368→}\n   369→\n   370→func ExtractSelectors(expr Expr) [][]*labels.Matcher {\n   371→\tvar selectors [][]*labels.Matcher\n   372→\tInspect(expr, func(node Node, _ []Node) error {\n   373→\t\tvs, ok := node.(*VectorSelector)\n   374→\t\tif ok {\n   375→\t\t\tselectors = append(selectors, vs.LabelMatchers)\n   376→\t\t}\n   377→\t\treturn nil\n   378→\t})\n   379→\treturn selectors\n   380→}\n   381→\n   382→type inspector func(Node, []Node) error\n   383→\n   384→func (f inspector) Visit(node Node, path []Node) (Visitor, error) {\n   385→\tif err := f(node, path); err != nil {\n   386→\t\treturn nil, err\n   387→\t}\n   388→\n   389→\treturn f, nil\n   390→}\n   391→\n   392→// Inspect traverses an AST in depth-first order: It starts by calling\n   393→// f(node, path); node must not be nil. it.\n   396→func Inspect(node Node, f inspector) {\n   397→\tvar pathBuf [4]Node        // To reduce allocations during recursion.\n   398→\tWalk(f, node, pathBuf[:0]) //nolint:errcheck\n   399→}\n   400→\n   401→// ChildrenIter returns an iterator over all child nodes of a syntax tree node.\n   402→func ChildrenIter(node Node) func(func(Node) bool) {\n   403→\treturn func(yield func(Node) bool) The Visit method is\n// invoked for each node with the path leading to the node provided additionally.\n// If the result visitor w is not nil and no error, Walk visits each of the children\n// of node with the visitor w, followed by a call of w.Visit(nil, nil).\ntype Visitor interface {\n\tVisit(node Node, path []Node) (w Visitor, err error)\n}\n\n// Walk traverses an AST in depth-first order: It starts by calling\n// v.Visit(node, path); node must not be nil. If the visitor w returned by\n// v.Visit(node, path) is not nil and the visitor returns no error, Walk is\n// invoked recursively with visitor w for each of the non-nil children of node,\n// followed by a call of w.Visit(nil), returning an error\n// As the tree is descended the path of previous nodes is provided.\nfunc Walk(v Visitor, node Node, path []Node) error {\n\tvar err error\n\tif v, err = v.Visit(node, path); v == nil || err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\tvar pathToHere []Node // Initialized only when needed.\n\n\tfor e := range ChildrenIter(node) {\n\t\tif pathToHere == nil {\n\t\t\tpathToHere = append(path, node)\n\t\t}\n\t\tif err := Walk(v, e, pathToHere); err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t_, err = v.Visit(nil, nil)\n\treturn err\n}\n\nfunc ExtractSelectors(expr Expr) [][]*labels.Matcher {\n\tvar selectors [][]*labels.Matcher\n\tInspect(expr, func(node Node, _ []Node) error {\n\t\tvs, ok := node.(*VectorSelector)\n\t\tif ok {\n\t\t\tselectors = append(selectors, vs.LabelMatchers)\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn nil\n\t})\n\treturn selectors\n}\n\ntype inspector func(Node, []Node) error\n\nfunc (f inspector) Visit(node Node, path []Node) (Visitor, error) {\n\tif err := f(node, path); err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\n\treturn f, nil\n}\n\n// Inspect traverses an AST in depth-first order: It starts by calling\n// f(node, path); node must not be nil.  299→func (p *parser) addParseErr(positionRange posrange.PositionRange, err error) {\n   300→\tperr := ParseErr{\n   301→\t\tPositionRange: positionRange,\n   302→\t\tErr:           err,\n 310→\tp.addParseErr(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), err)\n   311→}\n   312→\n   313→// unexpected creates a parser error complaining about an unexpected lexer item.\n   314→// The item that is presented as unexpected is always the last item produced\n   315→// by the lexer.\n   316→func (p *parser) unexpected(context, expected string) {\n   317→\tvar errMsg strings.Builder\n   318→\n   319→\t// Do not report lexer errors twice\n   320→\tif p.yyParser.lval.item.Typ == ERROR {\n   321→\t\treturn\n   322→\t}\n   323→\n   324→\terrMsg.WriteString(\"unexpected \")\n   325→\terrMsg.WriteString(p.yyParser.lval.item.desc())\n   326→\n   327→\tif context != \"\" {\n   328→\t\terrMsg.WriteString(\" in \")\n   329→\t\terrMsg.WriteString(context)\n   330→\t}\n   331→\n   332→\tif expected != \"\" {\n   333→\t\terrMsg.WriteString(\", expected \")\n   334→\t\terrMsg.WriteString(expected)\n   335→\t}\n   336→\n   337→\tp.addParseErr(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), errors.New(errMsg.String()))\n   338→}\n   339→\n   340→var errUnexpected = errors.New(\"unexpected error\")\n   341→\n   342→// recover is the handler that turns panics into returns from the top level of Parse.\n   343→func (*parser) recover(errp *error) {\n   344→\te := recover()\n   345→\tswitch _, ok := e.(runtime.Error); {\n   346→\tcase ok:\n   347→\t\t// Print the stack trace but do not inhibit the running application.\n   348→\t\tbuf := make([]byte, 64<<10)\n   349→\t\tbuf = buf[:runtime.Stack(buf, false)]\n   350→\n   351→\t\tfmt.Fprintf(os.Stderr, \"parser panic: %v\\n%s\", e, buf)\n   352→\t\t*errp = errUnexpected\n   353→\tcase e != nil:\n   354→\t\t*errp = e.(error)\n   355→\t}\n   356→}\n   357→\n   358→// Lex is expected by the yyLexer interface of the yacc generated parser.\n   359→// It writes the next Item provided by the lexer to the provided pointer address.\n   360→// Comments are skipped.\n   361→//\n   362→// The yyLexer interface is currently implemented by the parser to allow\n   363→// the generated and non-generated parts to work together with regards to lookahead\n   364→// and error handling.\n   365→//\n   366→// For more information, see https://pkg.go.dev/golang.org/x/tools/cmd/goyacc.\n   367→func (p *parser) Lex(lval *yySymType) int {\n   368→\tvar typ ItemType\n   369→\n   370→\tif p.injecting {\n   371→\t\tp.injecting = false\n   372→\t\treturn int(p.inject)\n   373→\t}\n   374→\t// Skip comments.\n   375→\tfor {\n   376→\t\tp.lex.NextItem(&lval.item)\n   377→\t\ttyp = lval.item.Typ\n   378→\t\tif typ != COMMENT {\n   379→\t\t\tbreak\n   380→\t\t}\n   381→\t}\n   382→\n   383→\tswitch typ {\n   384→\tcase ERROR:\n   385→\t\tpos := posrange.PositionRange{\n   386→\t\t\tStart: p.lex.start,\n   387→\t\t\tEnd:   posrange.Pos(len(p.lex.input)),\n   388→\t\t}\n   389→\t\tp.addParseErr(pos, errors.New(p.yyParser.lval.item.Val))\n   390→\n   391→\t\t// Tells yacc that this is the end of input.\n   392→\t\treturn 0\n   393→\tcase EOF:\n   394→\t\tlval.item.Typ = EOF\n   395→\t\tp.InjectItem(0)\n   396→\tcase RIGHT_BRACE, RIGHT_PAREN, RIGHT_BRACKET, DURATION, NUMBER:\n   397→\t\tp.lastClosing = lval.item.Pos + posrange.Pos(len(lval.item.Val))\n   398→\t}\n   399→\n   400→\treturn int(typ)\n   401→}\n   402→\n   403→// Error is expected by the yyLexer interface of the yacc generated parser.\n   404→//\n   405→// It is a no-op since the parsers error routines are triggered\n   406→// by mechanisms that allow more fine-grained control\n   407→// For more information, see https://pkg.go.dev/golang.org/x/tools/cmd/goyacc.\n   408→func (*parser) Error(string) {\n   409→}\n   410→\n   411→// InjectItem allows injecting a single Item at the beginning of the token stream\n   412→// consumed by the generated parser.\n   413→// This allows having multiple start symbols as described in\n   414→// https://www.gnu.org/software/bison/manual/html_node/Multiple-start_002dsymbols.html .\n   415→// Only the Lex function used by the generated parser is affected by this injected Item.\n   416→// Trying to inject when a previously injected Item has not yet been consumed will panic.\n   417→// Only Item types that are supposed to be used as start symbols are allowed as an argument.\n   418→func (p *parser) InjectItem(typ ItemType) {\n   419→\tif p.injecting {\n   420→\t\tpanic(\"cannot inject multiple Items into the token stream\")\n   421→\t}\n   422→\n   423→\tif typ != 0 && (typ <= startSymbolsStart || typ >= startSymbolsEnd) {\n   424→\t\tpanic(\"cannot inject symbol that isn't start symbol\")\n   425→\t}\n   426→\n   427→\tp.inject = typ\n   428→\tp.injecting = true\n   429→}\n   430→\n   431→func (p *parser) newBinaryExpression(lhs Node, op Item, modifiers, rhs Node) *BinaryExpr {\n   432→\tret := modifiers.(*BinaryExpr)\n   433→\n   434→\tret.LHS = lhs.(Expr)\n   435→\tret.RHS = rhs.(Expr)\n   436→\tret.Op = op.Typ\n   437→\n   438→\tif !p.options.EnableBinopFillModifiers && (ret.VectorMatching.FillValues.LHS != nil || ret.VectorMatching.FillValues.RHS != nil) {\n   439→\t\tp.addParseErrf(ret.PositionRange(), \"binop fill modifiers are experimental and not enabled\")\n   440→\t\treturn ret\n   441→\t}\n   442→\n   443→\treturn ret\n   444→}\n   445→\n   446→func (*parser) assembleVectorSelector(vs *VectorSelector) {\n   447→\t// If the metric name was set outside the braces, add a matcher for it.\n   448→\t// If the metric name was inside the braces we don't need to do anything.\n   449→\tif vs.Name != \"\" {\n   450→\t\tnameMatcher, err := labels.NewMatcher(labels.MatchEqual, labels.MetricName, vs.Name)\n   451→\t\tif err != nil {\n   452→\t\t\tpanic(err) // Must not happen with labels.MatchEqual\n   453→\t\t}\n   454→\t\tvs.LabelMatchers = append(vs.LabelMatchers, nameMatcher)\n   455→\t}\n   456→}\n   457→\n   458→func (p *parser) newAggregateExpr(op Item, modifier, args Node, overread bool) (ret *AggregateExpr) {\n   459→\tret = modifier.(*AggregateExpr)\n   460→\targuments := args.(Expressions)\n   461→\n   462→\tret.PosRange = posrange.PositionRange{\n   463→\t\tStart: op.Pos,\n   464→\t\tEnd:   p.lastClosing,\n   465→\t}\n   466→\tif overread {\n   467→\t\tret.PosRange.End = p.lex.findPrevRightParen(p.lastClosing)\n   468→\t}\n   469→\n   470→\tret.Op = op.Typ\n   471→\n   472→\tif len(arguments) == 0 {\n   473→\t\tp.addParseErrf(ret.PositionRange(), \"no arguments for aggregate expression provided\")\n   474→\n   475→\t\t// Prevents invalid array accesses.\n   476→\t\treturn ret\n   477→\t}\n   478→\n   479→\tdesiredArgs := 1\n   480→\tif ret.Op.IsAggregatorWithParam() {\n   481→\t\tif !p.options.EnableExperimentalFunctions && ret.Op.IsExperimentalAggregator() {\n   482→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(ret.PositionRange(), \"%s() is experimental and must be enabled with --enable-feature=promql-experimental-functions\", ret.Op)\n   483→\t\t\treturn ret\n   484→\t\t}\n   485→\t\tdesiredArgs = 2\n   486→\n   487→\t\tret.Param = arguments[0]\n   488→\t}\n   489→\n   490→\tif len(arguments) != desiredArgs {\n   491→\t\tp.addParseErrf(ret.PositionRange(), \"wrong number of arguments for aggregate expression provided, expected %d, got %d\", desiredArgs, len(arguments))\n   492→\t\treturn ret\n   493→\t}\n   494→\n   495→\tret.Expr = arguments[desiredArgs-1]\n   496→\n   497→\treturn ret\n   498→}\n   499→\n   500→// newMap is used when building the FloatHistogram from a map.\n   501→func (*parser) newMap() (ret map[string]any) {\n   502→\treturn map[string]any{}\n   503→}\n   504→\n   505→// mergeMaps is used to combine maps as they're used to later build the Float histogram.\n   506→// This will merge the right map into the left map.\n   507→func (p *parser) mergeMaps(left, right *map[string]any) (ret *map[string]any) {\n   508→\tfor key, value := range *right {\n   509→\t\tif _, ok := (*left)[key]; ok {\n   510→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(posrange.PositionRange{}, \"duplicate key \\\"%s\\\" in histogram\", key)\n   511→\t\t\tcontinue\n   512→\t\t}\n   513→\t\t(*left)[key] = value\n   514→\t}\n   515→\treturn left\n   516→}\n   517→\n   518→func (p *parser) histogramsIncreaseSeries(base, inc *histogram.FloatHistogram, times uint64) ([]SequenceValue, error) {\n   519→\t// Capture the hint set flag immediately after inc histogram is built.\n   520→\t// The base histogram's hint set flag was already captured.\n   521→\thintSet := p.lastHistogramCounterResetHintSet\n   522→\treturn p.histogramsSeries(base, inc, times, hintSet, func(a, b *histogram.FloatHistogram) (*histogram.FloatHistogram, error) {\n   523→\t\tres, _, _, err := a.Add(b)\n   524→\t\treturn res, err\n   525→\t})\n   526→}\n   527→\n   528→func (p *parser) histogramsDecreaseSeries(base, inc *histogram.FloatHistogram, times uint64) ([]SequenceValue, error) {\n   529→\t// Capture the hint set flag immediately after inc histogram is built.\n   530→\thintSet := p.lastHistogramCounterResetHintSet\n   531→\treturn p.histogramsSeries(base, inc, times, hintSet, func(a, b *histogram.FloatHistogram) (*histogram.FloatHistogram, error) {\n   532→\t\tres, _, _, err := a.Sub(b)\n   533→\t\treturn res, err\n   534→\t})\n   535→}\n   536→\n   537→func (*parser) histogramsSeries(base, inc *histogram.FloatHistogram, times uint64, counterResetHintSet bool,\n   538→\tcombine func(*histogram.FloatHistogram, *histogram.FloatHistogram) (*histogram.FloatHistogram, error),\n   539→) ([]SequenceValue, error) {\n   540→\tret := make([]SequenceValue, times+1)\n   541→\t// Add an additional value (the base) for time 0, which we ignore in tests.\n   542→\tret[0] = SequenceValue{Histogram: base, CounterResetHintSet: counterResetHintSet}\n   543→\tcur := base\n   544→\tfor i := uint64(1); i <= times; i++ {\n   545→\t\tif cur.Schema > inc.Schema {\n   546→\t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"error combining histograms: cannot merge from schema %d to %d\", inc.Schema, cur.Schema)\n   547→\t\t}\n   548→\n   549→\t\tvar err error\n   550→\t\tcur, err = combine(cur.Copy(), inc)\n   551→\t\tif err != nil {\n   552→\t\t\treturn ret, err\n   553→\t\t}\n   554→\t\tret[i] = SequenceValue{Histogram: cur, CounterResetHintSet: counterResetHintSet}\n   555→\t}\n   556→\n   557→\treturn ret, nil\n   558→}\n   559→\n   560→// buildHistogramFromMap is used in the grammar to take then individual parts of the histogram and complete it.\n   561→func (p *parser) buildHistogramFromMap(desc *map[string]any) *histogram.FloatHistogram {\n   562→\toutput := &histogram.FloatHistogram{}\n   563→\t// Reset the flag for each new histogram being built.\n   564→\tp.lastHistogramCounterResetHintSet = false\n   565→\n   566→\tval, ok := (*desc)[\"schema\"]\n   567→\tif ok {\n   568→\t\tschema, ok := val.(int64)\n   569→\t\tif ok {\n   570→\t\t\toutput.Schema = int32(schema)\n   571→\t\t} else {\n 590→\t\t} else {\n   591→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing count number: %v\", val)\n   592→\t\t}\n   593→\t}\n   594→\n   595→\tval, ok = 601→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing z_bucket number: %v\", val)\n   602→\t\t}\n   603→\t}\n   604→\tval, ok = (*desc)[\"z_bucket_w\"]\n   605→\tif ok {\n 626→\t\tp.lastHistogramCounterResetHintSet = true\n   627→\t\tresetHint, ok := val.(Item)\n   628→\n   629→\t\tif ok {\n   630→\t\t\tswitch resetHint.Typ {\n   631→\t\t\tcase UNKNOWN_COUNTER_RESET:\n 643→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing counter_reset_hint: %v\", val)\n   644→\t\t}\n   645→\t}\n   646→\n   647→\tbuckets, spans := 657→\n   658→// newHistogramSequenceValue creates a SequenceValue for a histogram,\n   659→// setting CounterResetHintSet based on whether counter_reset_hint was\n   660→// explicitly specified in the histogram description.\n   661→func (p *parser) newHistogramSequenceValue(h *histogram.FloatHistogram) SequenceValue {\n   662→\treturn SequenceValue{\n   663→\t\tHistogram:           h,\n   664→\t\tCounterResetHintSet: p.lastHistogramCounterResetHintSet,\n   665→\t}\n   666→}\n   667→\n   668→func (p *parser) buildHistogramBucketsAndSpans(desc *map[string]any, bucketsKey, offsetKey 674→\t\tif ok {\n   675→\t\t\tbuckets = val\n   676→\t\t\tbucketCount = len(buckets)\n   677→\t\t} else {\n   678→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing %s float 691→\tif bucketCount > 0 {\n   692→\t\tspans = []histogram.Span{{Offset: offset, Length: uint32(bucketCount)}}\n   693→\t}\n   694→\treturn buckets, spans\n   695→}\n   696→\n   697→// number parses a number.\n   698→func (p *parser) number(val string) float64 {\n   699→\tn, err := strconv.ParseInt(val, 0, 64)\n   700→\tf := float64(n)\n   701→\tif err != nil {\n   702→\t\tf, err = 708→}\n   709→\n   710→// expectType checks the type of the node and raises an error if it\n   711→// is not of the expected type.\n   712→func (p *parser) expectType(node Node, want ValueType, context string) {\n   713→\tt := p.checkAST(node)\n   714→\tif t != want {\n   715→\t\tp.addParseErrf(node.PositionRange(), \"expected type %s in %s, got %s\", DocumentedType(want), context, DocumentedType(t))\n   716→\t}\n   717→}\n   718→\n   719→// checkAST checks the validity of the provided AST. This includes type checking.\n   720→func (p *parser) checkAST(node Node) (typ ValueType) {\n   721→\t// For expressions the type is determined by their Type function.\n   722→\t// Lists do not have a type but are not invalid either.\n   723→\tswitch n := node.(type) {\n   724→\tcase Expressions:\n   725→\t\ttyp = ValueTypeNone\n   726→\tcase Expr:\n   727→\t\ttyp = n.Type()\n   728→\tdefault:\n   729→\t\tp.addParseErrf(node.PositionRange(), \"unknown node type: %T\", node)\n   730→\t}\n   731→\n   732→\t// Recursively check correct typing for child nodes and raise\n   733→\t// errors in case of bad typing.\n   734→\tswitch n := node.(type) {\n   735→\tcase *EvalStmt:\n   736→\t\tty := p.checkAST(n.Expr)\n   737→\t\tif ty == ValueTypeNone {\n   738→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.Expr.PositionRange(), \"evaluation statement must have a valid expression type but got %s\", DocumentedType(ty))\n   739→\t\t}\n   740→\n   741→\tcase Expressions:\n   742→\t\tfor _, e := range n {\n   743→\t\t\tty := p.checkAST(e)\n   744→\t\t\tif ty == ValueTypeNone {\n   745→\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(e.PositionRange(), \"expression must have a valid expression type but got %s\", DocumentedType(ty))\n   746→\t\t\t}\n   747→\t\t}\n   748→\tcase *AggregateExpr:\n   749→\t\tif !n.Op.IsAggregator() {\n   750→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"aggregation operator expected in aggregation expression but got %q\", n.Op)\n   751→\t\t}\n   752→\t\tp.expectType(n.Expr, ValueTypeVector, \"aggregation expression\")\n   753→\t\tif n.Op == TOPK || n.Op == BOTTOMK || n.Op == QUANTILE || n.Op == LIMITK || n.Op == LIMIT_RATIO {\n   754→\t\t\tp.expectType(n.Param, ValueTypeScalar, \"aggregation parameter\")\n   755→\t\t}\n   756→\t\tif n.Op == COUNT_VALUES {\n   757→\t\t\tp.expectType(n.Param, ValueTypeString, \"aggregation parameter\")\n   758→\t\t}\n   759→\n   760→\tcase *BinaryExpr:\n   761→\t\tlt := p.checkAST(n.LHS)\n   762→\t\trt := p.checkAST(n.RHS)\n   763→\n   764→\t\t// opRange returns the PositionRange of the operator part of the BinaryExpr.\n   765→\t\t// This is made a function instead of a variable, so it is lazily evaluated on demand.\n   766→\t\topRange := func() (r posrange.PositionRange) {\n   767→\t\t\t// Remove whitespace at the beginning and end of the range.\n   768→\t\t\tfor r.Start = n.LHS.PositionRange().End; isSpace(rune(p.lex.input[r.Start])); r.Start++ {\n   769→\t\t\t}\n   770→\t\t\tfor r.End = n.RHS.PositionRange().Start - 1; isSpace(rune(p.lex.input[r.End])); r.End-- {\n   771→\t\t\t}\n   772→\t\t\treturn r\n   773→\t\t}\n   774→\n   775→\t\tif n.ReturnBool && !n.Op.IsComparisonOperator() {\n   776→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(opRange(), \"bool modifier can only be used on comparison operators\")\n   777→\t\t}\n   778→\n   779→\t\tif n.Op.IsComparisonOperator() && !n.ReturnBool && n.RHS.Type() == ValueTypeScalar && n.LHS.Type() == ValueTypeScalar {\n   780→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(opRange(), \"comparisons between scalars must use BOOL modifier\")\n   781→\t\t}\n   782→\n   783→\t\tif n.Op.IsSetOperator() && n.VectorMatching.Card == CardOneToOne {\n   784→\t\t\tn.VectorMatching.Card = CardManyToMany\n   785→\t\t}\n   786→\n   787→\t\tfor _, l1 := range n.VectorMatching.MatchingLabels {\n   788→\t\t\tfor _, l2 := range n.VectorMatching.Include {\n   789→\t\t\t\tif l1 == l2 && n.VectorMatching.On {\n   790→\t\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(opRange(), \"label %q must not occur in ON and GROUP clause at once\", l1)\n   791→\t\t\t\t}\n   792→\t\t\t}\n   793→\t\t}\n   794→\n   795→\t\tif !n.Op.IsOperator() {\n   796→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"binary expression does not support operator %q\", n.Op)\n   797→\t\t}\n   798→\t\tif lt != ValueTypeScalar && lt != ValueTypeVector {\n   799→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.LHS.PositionRange(), \"binary expression must contain only scalar and instant vector types\")\n   800→\t\t}\n   801→\t\tif rt != ValueTypeScalar && rt != ValueTypeVector {\n   802→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.RHS.PositionRange(), \"binary expression must contain only scalar and instant vector types\")\n   803→\t\t}\n   804→\n   805→\t\tswitch {\n   806→\t\tcase (lt != ValueTypeVector || rt != ValueTypeVector) && n.VectorMatching != nil:\n   807→\t\t\tif len(n.VectorMatching.MatchingLabels) > 0 {\n   808→\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"vector matching only allowed between instant vectors\")\n   809→\t\t\t}\n   810→\t\t\tif n.VectorMatching.FillValues.LHS != nil || n.VectorMatching.FillValues.RHS != nil {\n   811→\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"filling in missing series only allowed between instant vectors\")\n   812→\t\t\t}\n   813→\t\t\tn.VectorMatching = nil\n   814→\t\tcase n.Op.IsSetOperator(): // Both operands are Vectors.\n   815→\t\t\tif n.VectorMatching.Card == CardOneToMany || n.VectorMatching.Card == CardManyToOne {\n   816→\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"no grouping allowed for %q operation\", n.Op)\n   817→\t\t\t}\n   818→\t\t\tif n.VectorMatching.Card != CardManyToMany {\n   819→\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"set operations must always be many-to-many\")\n   820→\t\t\t}\n   821→\t\t\tif n.VectorMatching.FillValues.LHS != nil || n.VectorMatching.FillValues.RHS != nil {\n   822→\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"filling in missing series not allowed for set operators\")\n   823→\t\t\t}\n   824→\t\t}\n   825→\n   826→\t\tif (lt == ValueTypeScalar || rt == ValueTypeScalar) && n.Op.IsSetOperator() {\n   827→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"set operator %q not allowed in binary scalar expression\", n.Op)\n   828→\t\t}\n   829→\n   830→\tcase *Call:\n   831→\t\tnargs := len(n.Func.ArgTypes)\n   832→\t\tif n.Func.Variadic == 0 {\n   833→\t\t\tif nargs != len(n.Args) {\n   834→\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"expected %d argument(s) in call to %q, got %d\", nargs, n.Func.Name, len(n.Args))\n   835→\t\t\t}\n   836→\t\t} else {\n   837→\t\t\tna := nargs - 1\n   838→\t\t\tif na > len(n.Args) {\n   839→\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"expected at least %d argument(s) in call to %q, got %d\", na, n.Func.Name, len(n.Args))\n   840→\t\t\t} else if nargsmax := na + n.Func.Variadic; n.Func.Variadic > 0 && nargsmax < len(n.Args) {\n   841→\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"expected at most %d argument(s) in call to %q, got %d\", nargsmax, n.Func.Name, len(n.Args))\n   842→\t\t\t}\n   843→\t\t}\n   844→\n   845→\t\tif n.Func.Name == \"info\" && len(n.Args) > 1 {\n   846→\t\t\t// Check the type is correct first\n   847→\t\t\tif n.Args[1].Type() != ValueTypeVector {\n   848→\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(node.PositionRange(), \"expected type %s in %s, got %s\", DocumentedType(ValueTypeVector), fmt.Sprintf(\"call to function %q\", n.Func.Name), DocumentedType(n.Args[1].Type()))\n   849→\t\t\t}\n   850→\t\t\t// Check the vector selector in the input doesn't contain a metric name\n   851→\t\t\tif vs, ok := n.Args[1].(*VectorSelector); ok && vs.Name != \"\" {\n   852→\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.Args[1].PositionRange(), \"expected label selectors only, got vector selector instead\")\n   853→\t\t\t} else if ok {\n   854→\t\t\t\t// Set Vector Selector flag to bypass empty matcher check\n   855→\t\t\t\tvs.BypassEmptyMatcherCheck = true\n   856→\t\t\t} else {\n   857→\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.Args[1].PositionRange(), \"expected label selectors only\")\n   858→\t\t\t}\n   859→\t\t}\n   860→\n   861→\t\tfor i, arg := range n.Args {\n   862→\t\t\tif i >= len(n.Func.ArgTypes) {\n   863→\t\t\t\tif n.Func.Variadic == 0 {\n   864→\t\t\t\t\t// This is not a vararg function so we should not check the\n   865→\t\t\t\t\t// type of the extra arguments.\n   866→\t\t\t\t\tbreak\n   867→\t\t\t\t}\n   868→\t\t\t\ti = len(n.Func.ArgTypes) - 1\n   869→\t\t\t}\n   870→\t\t\tif t := p.checkAST(arg); t != n.Func.ArgTypes[i] {\n   871→\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(arg.PositionRange(), \"expected type %s in call to function %q, got %s\", DocumentedType(n.Func.ArgTypes[i]), n.Func.Name, DocumentedType(t))\n   872→\t\t\t}\n   873→\t\t}\n   874→\n   875→\tcase *ParenExpr:\n   876→\t\tp.checkAST(n.Expr)\n   877→\n   878→\tcase *UnaryExpr:\n   879→\t\tif n.Op != ADD && n.Op != SUB {\n   880→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"only + and - operators allowed for unary expressions\")\n   881→\t\t}\n   882→\t\tif t := %q\", DocumentedType(t))\n   884→\t\t}\n   885→\n   886→\tcase *SubqueryExpr:\n   887→\t\tty := p.checkAST(n.Expr)\n   888→\t\tif ty != ValueTypeVector {\n   889→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"subquery is only allowed on instant vector, got %s instead\", ty)\n   890→\t\t}\n   891→\tcase *MatrixSelector:\n   892→\t\tp.checkAST(n.VectorSelector)\n   893→\n   894→\tcase *VectorSelector:\n   895→\t\tif n.Name != \"\" {\n   896→\t\t\t// In this case the last LabelMatcher is checking for the metric name\n   897→\t\t\t// set outside the braces. labels.MetricName {\n   901→\t\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"metric name must not be set twice: %q or %q\", n.Name, m.Value)\n   902→\t\t\t\t}\n   903→\t\t\t}\n   904→\n   905→\t\t\t// 910→\t\t\t// A Vector selector must contain at least one non-empty matcher to prevent\n   911→\t\t\t// implicit selection of all metrics (e.g. by a typo).\n   912→\t\t\tnotEmpty := false\n   913→\t\t\tfor _, lm := range n.LabelMatchers {\n   914→\t\t\t\tif lm != nil && !lm.Matches(\"\") {\n   915→\t\t\t\t\tnotEmpty = true\n   916→\t\t\t\t\tbreak\n   917→\t\t\t\t}\n   918→\t\t\t}\n   919→\t\t\tif !notEmpty {\n   920→\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"vector selector must contain at least one non-empty matcher\")\n   921→\t\t\t}\n   922→\t\t}\n   923→\n   924→\tcase *NumberLiteral, *StringLiteral:\n   925→\t\t// Nothing to do for terminals.\n   926→\n   927→\tdefault:\n   928→\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"unknown node type: %T\", node)\n   929→\t}\n   930→\treturn typ\n   931→}\n   932→\n   933→func (p *parser) unquoteString(s string) string {\n   934→\tunquoted, err := strutil.Unquote(s)\n   935→\tif err != nil {\n   936→\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error unquoting string %q: %s\", s, err)\n   937→\t}\n   938→\treturn unquoted\n   939→}\n   940→\n   941→func parseDuration(ds string) set to true when the most recently\n\t// built histogram had a counter_reset_hint explicitly specified.\n\t// This is used to populate CounterResetHintSet in SequenceValue.\n\tlastHistogramCounterResetHintSet bool\n\n\toptions Options\n}\n\n// newParser returns a new low-level parser instance from the pool.\nfunc newParser(input string, opts Options) *parser {\n\tp := parserPool.Get().(*parser)\n\n\tp.functions = Functions\n\tp.injecting = false\n\tp.parseErrors = nil\n\tp.generatedParserResult = nil\n\tp.lastClosing = posrange.Pos(0)\n\tp.options = opts\n\n\t// Clear lexer struct before reusing.\n\tp.lex = Lexer{\n\t\tinput: input,\n\t\tstate: lexStatements,\n\t}\n\n\treturn p\n}\n\n// newParserWithFunctions returns a new low-level parser p\n}\n\nfunc (p *parser) parseExpr() (expr Expr, err error) {\n\tdefer p.recover(&err)\n\n\tparseResult := p.parseGenerated(START_EXPRESSION)\n\n\tif parseResult != nil {\n\t\texpr = Only used inside unit tests.\n\tLineOffset int\n}\n\nfunc (e *ParseErr) Error() string {\n\treturn fmt.Sprintf(\"%s: parse error: %s\", e.PositionRange.StartPosInput(e.Query, e.LineOffset), e.Err)\n}\n\ntype ParseErrors []ParseErr\n\n// Since producing multiple error messages might look weird when combined with error wrapping,\n// only the first error produced by the parser is included in the error string.\n// If getting the full error list is desired, it is recommended to typecast the error returned\n// by the parser to ParseErrors and work with the underlying slice.\nfunc (errs ParseErrors) Error() string {\n\tif len(errs) != 0 {\n\t\treturn errs[0].Error()\n\t}\n\t// Should never happen\n\t// Panicking while printing an error seems like a bad idea, so the\n\t// situation is explained in the error message instead.\n\treturn \"error contains no error message\"\n}\n\n// EnrichParseError enriches a single or list of parse errors (used for unit tests and promtool).\nfunc EnrichParseError(err error, enrich func(parseErr *ParseErr)) {\n\tvar parseErr *ParseErr\n\tif errors.As(err, &parseErr) {\n\t\tenrich(parseErr)\n\t}\n\tvar parseErrors ParseErrors\n\tif errors.As(err, &parseErrors) {\n\t\tfor i, e := range parseErrors {\n\t\t\tenrich(&e)\n\t\t\tparseErrors[i] = e\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n\n// SequenceValue is an omittable value in a sequence of time series values.\ntype SequenceValue struct {\n\tValue     float64\n\tOmitted   bool\n\tHistogram *histogram.FloatHistogram\n\t// CounterResetHintSet is true if the counter reset hint was explicitly\n\t// specified in the test file using counter_reset_hint:... syntax.\n\t// This allows distinguishing between \"no hint specified\" (don't care)\n\t// vs \"counter_reset_hint:unknown\" (verify it's unknown).\n\tCounterResetHintSet bool\n}\n\nfunc (v SequenceValue) String() string {\n\tif v.Omitted {\n\t\treturn \"_\"\n\t}\n\tif v.Histogram != nil {\n\t\treturn v.Histogram.String()\n\t}\n\treturn fmt.Sprintf(\"%f\", v.Value)\n}\n\ntype seriesDescription struct {\n\tlabels labels.Labels\n\tvalues []SequenceValue\n}\n\n// addParseErrf formats the error and appends it to the list of parsing errors.\nfunc (p *parser) addParseErrf(positionRange posrange.PositionRange, format string, args ...any) {\n\tp.addParseErr(positionRange, fmt.Errorf(format, args...))\n}\n\n// addParseErr appends the provided error to the list of parsing errors.\nfunc (p *parser) addParseErr(positionRange posrange.PositionRange, err error) {\n\tperr := ParseErr{\n\t\tPositionRange: positionRange,\n\t\tErr:           err,\n\t\tQuery:         p.lex.input,\n\t}\n\n\tp.parseErrors = append(p.parseErrors, perr)\n}\n\nfunc (p *parser) addSemanticError(err error) {\n\tp.addParseErr(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), err)\n}\n\n// unexpected creates a parser error complaining about an unexpected lexer item.\n// The item that is presented as unexpected is always the last item produced\n// by the lexer.\nfunc (p *parser) unexpected(context, expected string) {\n\tvar errMsg strings.Builder\n\n\t// Do not report lexer errors twice\n\tif p.yyParser.lval.item.Typ == ERROR {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\terrMsg.WriteString(\"unexpected \")\n\terrMsg.WriteString(p.yyParser.lval.item.desc())\n\n\tif context != \"\" {\n\t\terrMsg.WriteString(\" in \")\n\t\terrMsg.WriteString(context)\n\t}\n\n\tif expected != \"\" {\n\t\terrMsg.WriteString(\", expected \")\n\t\terrMsg.WriteString(expected)\n\t}\n\n\tp.addParseErr(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), errors.New(errMsg.String()))\n}\n\nvar errUnexpected = errors.New(\"unexpected error\")\n\n// recover is the handler that turns panics into returns from the top level of Parse.\nfunc (*parser) recover(errp *error) {\n\te := recover()\n\tswitch _, ok := e.(runtime.Error); {\n\tcase ok:\n\t\t// Print the stack trace but do not inhibit the running application.\n\t\tbuf := make([]byte, 64<<10)\n\t\tbuf = buf[:runtime.Stack(buf, false)]\n\n\t\tfmt.Fprintf(os.Stderr, \"parser panic: %v\\n%s\", e, buf)\n\t\t*errp = errUnexpected\n\tcase e != nil:\n\t\t*errp = e.(error)\n\t}\n}\n\n// Lex is expected by the yyLexer interface of the yacc generated parser.\n// It writes the next Item provided by the lexer to the provided pointer address.\n// Comments are skipped.\n//\n// The yyLexer interface is currently implemented by the parser to allow\n// the generated and non-generated parts to work together with regards to lookahead\n// and error handling.\n//\n// For more information, see https://pkg.go.dev/golang.org/x/tools/cmd/goyacc.\nfunc (p *parser) Lex(lval *yySymType) int {\n\tvar typ ItemType\n\n\tif p.injecting {\n\t\tp.injecting = false\n\t\treturn int(p.inject)\n\t}\n\t// Skip comments.\n\tfor {\n\t\tp.lex.NextItem(&lval.item)\n\t\ttyp = lval.item.Typ\n\t\tif typ != COMMENT {\n\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tswitch typ {\n\tcase ERROR:\n\t\tpos := posrange.PositionRange{\n\t\t\tStart: p.lex.start,\n\t\t\tEnd:   posrange.Pos(len(p.lex.input)),\n\t\t}\n\t\tp.addParseErr(pos, errors.New(p.yyParser.lval.item.Val))\n\n\t\t// Tells yacc that this is the end of input.\n\t\treturn 0\n\tcase EOF:\n\t\tlval.item.Typ = EOF\n\t\tp.InjectItem(0)\n\tcase RIGHT_BRACE, RIGHT_PAREN, RIGHT_BRACKET, DURATION, NUMBER:\n\t\tp.lastClosing = lval.item.Pos + posrange.Pos(len(lval.item.Val))\n\t}\n\n\treturn int(typ)\n}\n\n// Error is expected by the yyLexer interface of the yacc generated parser.\n//\n// It is a no-op since the parsers error routines are triggered\n// by mechanisms that allow more fine-grained control\n// For more information, see https://pkg.go.dev/golang.org/x/tools/cmd/goyacc.\nfunc (*parser) Error(string) {\n}\n\n// InjectItem allows injecting a single Item at the beginning of the token stream\n// consumed by the generated parser.\n// This allows having multiple start symbols as described in\n// https://www.gnu.org/software/bison/manual/html_node/Multiple-start_002dsymbols.html .\n// Only the Lex function used by the generated parser is affected by this injected Item.\n// Trying to inject when a previously injected Item has not yet been consumed will panic.\n// Only Item types that are supposed to be used as start symbols are allowed as an argument.\nfunc (p *parser) InjectItem(typ ItemType) {\n\tif p.injecting {\n\t\tpanic(\"cannot inject multiple Items into the token stream\")\n\t}\n\n\tif typ != 0 && (typ <= startSymbolsStart || typ >= startSymbolsEnd) {\n\t\tpanic(\"cannot inject symbol that isn't start symbol\")\n\t}\n\n\tp.inject = typ\n\tp.injecting = true\n}\n\nfunc (p *parser) newBinaryExpression(lhs Node, op Item, modifiers, rhs Node) *BinaryExpr {\n\tret := modifiers.(*BinaryExpr)\n\n\tret.LHS = lhs.(Expr)\n\tret.RHS = rhs.(Expr)\n\tret.Op = op.Typ\n\n\tif !p.options.EnableBinopFillModifiers && (ret.VectorMatching.FillValues.LHS != nil || ret.VectorMatching.FillValues.RHS != nil) {\n\t\tp.addParseErrf(ret.PositionRange(), \"binop fill modifiers are experimental and not enabled\")\n\t\treturn ret\n\t}\n\n\treturn ret\n}\n\nfunc (*parser) assembleVectorSelector(vs *VectorSelector) {\n\t// If the metric name was set outside the braces, add a matcher for it.\n\t// If the metric name was inside the braces we don't need to do anything.\n\tif vs.Name != \"\" {\n\t\tnameMatcher, err := labels.NewMatcher(labels.MatchEqual, labels.MetricName, vs.Name)\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\tpanic(err) // Must not happen with labels.MatchEqual\n\t\t}\n\t\tvs.LabelMatchers = append(vs.LabelMatchers, nameMatcher)\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (p *parser) newAggregateExpr(op Item, modifier, args Node, overread bool) (ret *AggregateExpr) {\n\tret = modifier.(*AggregateExpr)\n\targuments := args.(Expressions)\n\n\tret.PosRange = posrange.PositionRange{\n\t\tStart: op.Pos,\n\t\tEnd:   p.lastClosing,\n\t}\n\tif overread {\n\t\tret.PosRange.End = p.lex.findPrevRightParen(p.lastClosing)\n\t}\n\n\tret.Op = op.Typ\n\n\tif len(arguments) == 0 {\n\t\tp.addParseErrf(ret.PositionRange(), \"no arguments for aggregate expression provided\")\n\n\t\t// Prevents invalid array accesses.\n\t\treturn ret\n\t}\n\n\tdesiredArgs := 1\n\tif ret.Op.IsAggregatorWithParam() {\n\t\tif !p.options.EnableExperimentalFunctions && ret.Op.IsExperimentalAggregator() {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(ret.PositionRange(), \"%s() is experimental and must be enabled with --enable-feature=promql-experimental-functions\", ret.Op)\n\t\t\treturn ret\n\t\t}\n\t\tdesiredArgs = 2\n\n\t\tret.Param = arguments[0]\n\t}\n\n\tif len(arguments) != desiredArgs {\n\t\tp.addParseErrf(ret.PositionRange(), \"wrong number of arguments for aggregate expression provided, expected %d, got %d\", desiredArgs, len(arguments))\n\t\treturn ret\n\t}\n\n\tret.Expr = arguments[desiredArgs-1]\n\n\treturn ret\n}\n\n// newMap is used when building the FloatHistogram from a map.\nfunc (*parser) newMap() (ret map[string]any) {\n\treturn map[string]any{}\n}\n\n// mergeMaps is used to combine maps as they're used to later build the Float histogram.\n// This will merge the right map into the left map.\nfunc (p *parser) mergeMaps(left, right *map[string]any) (ret *map[string]any) {\n\tfor key, value := range *right {\n\t\tif _, ok := (*left)[key]; ok {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(posrange.PositionRange{}, \"duplicate key \\\"%s\\\" in histogram\", key)\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\t\t(*left)[key] = value\n\t}\n\treturn left\n}\n\nfunc (p *parser) histogramsIncreaseSeries(base, inc *histogram.FloatHistogram, times uint64) ([]SequenceValue, error) {\n\t// Capture the hint set flag immediately after inc histogram is built.\n\t// The base histogram's hint set flag was already captured.\n\thintSet := p.lastHistogramCounterResetHintSet\n\treturn p.histogramsSeries(base, inc, times, hintSet, func(a, b *histogram.FloatHistogram) (*histogram.FloatHistogram, error) {\n\t\tres, _, _, err := a.Add(b)\n\t\treturn res, err\n\t})\n}\n\nfunc (p *parser) histogramsDecreaseSeries(base, inc *histogram.FloatHistogram, times uint64) ([]SequenceValue, error) {\n\t// Capture the hint set flag immediately after inc histogram is built.\n\thintSet := p.lastHistogramCounterResetHintSet\n\treturn p.histogramsSeries(base, inc, times, hintSet, func(a, b *histogram.FloatHistogram) (*histogram.FloatHistogram, error) {\n\t\tres, _, _, err := a.Sub(b)\n\t\treturn res, err\n\t})\n}\n\nfunc (*parser) histogramsSeries(base, inc *histogram.FloatHistogram, times uint64, counterResetHintSet bool,\n\tcombine func(*histogram.FloatHistogram, *histogram.FloatHistogram) (*histogram.FloatHistogram, error),\n) ([]SequenceValue, error) {\n\tret := make([]SequenceValue, times+1)\n\t// Add an additional value (the base) for time 0, which we ignore in tests.\n\tret[0] = SequenceValue{Histogram: base, CounterResetHintSet: counterResetHintSet}\n\tcur := base\n\tfor i := uint64(1); i <= times; i++ {\n\t\tif cur.Schema > inc.Schema {\n\t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"error combining histograms: cannot merge from schema %d to %d\", inc.Schema, cur.Schema)\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tvar err error\n\t\tcur, err = combine(cur.Copy(), inc)\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn ret, err\n\t\t}\n\t\tret[i] = SequenceValue{Histogram: cur, CounterResetHintSet: counterResetHintSet}\n\t}\n\n\treturn ret, nil\n}\n\n// buildHistogramFromMap is used in the grammar to take then individual parts of the histogram and complete it.\nfunc (p *parser) buildHistogramFromMap(desc *map[string]any) *histogram.FloatHistogram {\n\toutput := &histogram.FloatHistogram{}\n\t// Reset the flag for each new histogram being built.\n\tp.lastHistogramCounterResetHintSet = false\n\n\tval, ok := (*desc)[\"schema\"]\n\tif ok {\n\t\tschema, ok := val.(int64)\n\t\tif ok {\n\t\t\toutput.Schema = int32(schema)\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing schema number: %v\", val)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tval, ok = (*desc)[\"sum\"]\n\tif ok {\n\t\tsum, ok := val.(float64)\n\t\tif ok {\n\t\t\toutput.Sum = sum\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing sum number: %v\", val)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\tval, ok = (*desc)[\"count\"]\n\tif ok {\n\t\tcount, ok := val.(float64)\n\t\tif ok {\n\t\t\toutput.Count = count\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing count number: %v\", val)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tval, ok = (*desc)[\"z_bucket\"]\n\tif ok {\n\t\tbucket, ok := val.(float64)\n\t\tif ok {\n\t\t\toutput.ZeroCount = bucket\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing z_bucket number: %v\", val)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\tval, ok = (*desc)[\"z_bucket_w\"]\n\tif ok {\n\t\tbucketWidth, ok := val.(float64)\n\t\tif ok {\n\t\t\toutput.ZeroThreshold = bucketWidth\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing z_bucket_w number: %v\", val)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\tval, ok = (*desc)[\"custom_values\"]\n\tif ok {\n\t\tcustomValues, ok := val.([]float64)\n\t\tif ok {\n\t\t\toutput.CustomValues = customValues\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing custom_values: %v\", val)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tval, ok = (*desc)[\"counter_reset_hint\"]\n\tif ok {\n\t\t// Mark that the counter reset hint was explicitly specified.\n\t\tp.lastHistogramCounterResetHintSet = true\n\t\tresetHint, ok := val.(Item)\n\n\t\tif ok {\n\t\t\tswitch resetHint.Typ {\n\t\t\tcase UNKNOWN_COUNTER_RESET:\n\t\t\t\toutput.CounterResetHint = histogram.UnknownCounterReset\n\t\t\tcase COUNTER_RESET:\n\t\t\t\toutput.CounterResetHint = histogram.CounterReset\n\t\t\tcase NOT_COUNTER_RESET:\n\t\t\t\toutput.CounterResetHint = histogram.NotCounterReset\n\t\t\tcase GAUGE_TYPE:\n\t\t\t\toutput.CounterResetHint = histogram.GaugeType\n\t\t\tdefault:\n\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing counter_reset_hint: unknown value %v\", resetHint.Typ)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing counter_reset_hint: %v\", val)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tbuckets, spans := p.buildHistogramBucketsAndSpans(desc, \"buckets\", \"offset\")\n\toutput.PositiveBuckets = buckets\n\toutput.PositiveSpans = spans\n\n\tbuckets, spans = p.buildHistogramBucketsAndSpans(desc, \"n_buckets\", \"n_offset\")\n\toutput.NegativeBuckets = buckets\n\toutput.NegativeSpans = spans\n\n\treturn output\n}\n\n// newHistogramSequenceValue creates a SequenceValue for a histogram,\n// setting CounterResetHintSet based on whether counter_reset_hint was\n// explicitly specified in the histogram description.\nfunc (p *parser) newHistogramSequenceValue(h *histogram.FloatHistogram) SequenceValue {\n\treturn SequenceValue{\n\t\tHistogram:           h,\n\t\tCounterResetHintSet: p.lastHistogramCounterResetHintSet,\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (p *parser) buildHistogramBucketsAndSpans(desc *map[string]any, bucketsKey, offsetKey string,\n) (buckets []float64, spans []histogram.Span) {\n\tbucketCount := 0\n\tval, ok := (*desc)[bucketsKey]\n\tif ok {\n\t\tval, ok := val.([]float64)\n\t\tif ok {\n\t\t\tbuckets = val\n\t\t\tbucketCount = len(buckets)\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing %s float array: %v\", bucketsKey, val)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\toffset := int32(0)\n\tval, ok = (*desc)[offsetKey]\n\tif ok {\n\t\tval, ok := val.(int64)\n\t\tif ok {\n\t\t\toffset = int32(val)\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing %s number: %v\", offsetKey, val)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\tif bucketCount > 0 {\n\t\tspans = []histogram.Span{{Offset: offset, Length: uint32(bucketCount)}}\n\t}\n\treturn buckets, spans\n}\n\n// number parses a number.\nfunc (p *parser) number(val string) float64 {\n\tn, err := strconv.ParseInt(val, 0, 64)\n\tf := float64(n)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\tf, err = strconv.ParseFloat(val, 64)\n\t}\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing number: %s\", err)\n\t}\n\treturn f\n}\n\n// expectType checks the type of the node and raises an error if it\n// is not of the expected type.\nfunc (p *parser) expectType(node Node, want ValueType, context string) {\n\tt := p.checkAST(node)\n\tif t != want {\n\t\tp.addParseErrf(node.PositionRange(), \"expected type %s in %s, got %s\", DocumentedType(want), context, DocumentedType(t))\n\t}\n}\n\n// checkAST checks the validity of the provided AST. This includes type checking.\nfunc (p *parser) checkAST(node Node) (typ ValueType) {\n\t// For expressions the type is determined by their Type function.\n\t// Lists do not have a type but are not invalid either.\n\tswitch n := node.(type) {\n\tcase Expressions:\n\t\ttyp = ValueTypeNone\n\tcase Expr:\n\t\ttyp = n.Type()\n\tdefault:\n\t\tp.addParseErrf(node.PositionRange(), \"unknown node type: %T\", node)\n\t}\n\n\t// Recursively check correct typing for child nodes and raise\n\t// errors in case of bad typing.\n\tswitch n := node.(type) {\n\tcase *EvalStmt:\n\t\tty := p.checkAST(n.Expr)\n\t\tif ty == ValueTypeNone {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.Expr.PositionRange(), \"evaluation statement must have a valid expression type but got %s\", DocumentedType(ty))\n\t\t}\n\n\tcase Expressions:\n\t\tfor _, e := range n {\n\t\t\tty := p.checkAST(e)\n\t\t\tif ty == ValueTypeNone {\n\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(e.PositionRange(), \"expression must have a valid expression type but got %s\", DocumentedType(ty))\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\tcase *AggregateExpr:\n\t\tif !n.Op.IsAggregator() {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"aggregation operator expected in aggregation expression but got %q\", n.Op)\n\t\t}\n\t\tp.expectType(n.Expr, ValueTypeVector, \"aggregation expression\")\n\t\tif n.Op == TOPK || n.Op == BOTTOMK || n.Op == QUANTILE || n.Op == LIMITK || n.Op == LIMIT_RATIO {\n\t\t\tp.expectType(n.Param, ValueTypeScalar, \"aggregation parameter\")\n\t\t}\n\t\tif n.Op == COUNT_VALUES {\n\t\t\tp.expectType(n.Param, ValueTypeString, \"aggregation parameter\")\n\t\t}\n\n\tcase *BinaryExpr:\n\t\tlt := p.checkAST(n.LHS)\n\t\trt := p.checkAST(n.RHS)\n\n\t\t// opRange returns the PositionRange of the operator part of the BinaryExpr.\n\t\t// This is made a function instead of a variable, so it is lazily evaluated on demand.\n\t\topRange := func() (r posrange.PositionRange) {\n\t\t\t// Remove whitespace at the beginning and end of the range.\n\t\t\tfor r.Start = n.LHS.PositionRange().End; isSpace(rune(p.lex.input[r.Start])); r.Start++ {\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tfor r.End = n.RHS.PositionRange().Start - 1; isSpace(rune(p.lex.input[r.End])); r.End-- {\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\treturn r\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tif n.ReturnBool && !n.Op.IsComparisonOperator() {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(opRange(), \"bool modifier can only be used on comparison operators\")\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tif n.Op.IsComparisonOperator() && !n.ReturnBool && n.RHS.Type() == ValueTypeScalar && n.LHS.Type() == ValueTypeScalar {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(opRange(), \"comparisons between scalars must use BOOL modifier\")\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tif n.Op.IsSetOperator() && n.VectorMatching.Card == CardOneToOne {\n\t\t\tn.VectorMatching.Card = CardManyToMany\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tfor _, l1 := range n.VectorMatching.MatchingLabels {\n\t\t\tfor _, l2 := range n.VectorMatching.Include {\n\t\t\t\tif l1 == l2 && n.VectorMatching.On {\n\t\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(opRange(), \"label %q must not occur in ON and GROUP clause at once\", l1)\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tif !n.Op.IsOperator() {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"binary expression does not support operator %q\", n.Op)\n\t\t}\n\t\tif lt != ValueTypeScalar && lt != ValueTypeVector {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.LHS.PositionRange(), \"binary expression must contain only scalar and instant vector types\")\n\t\t}\n\t\tif rt != ValueTypeScalar && rt != ValueTypeVector {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.RHS.PositionRange(), \"binary expression must contain only scalar and instant vector types\")\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tswitch {\n\t\tcase (lt != ValueTypeVector || rt != ValueTypeVector) && n.VectorMatching != nil:\n\t\t\tif len(n.VectorMatching.MatchingLabels) > 0 {\n\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"vector matching only allowed between instant vectors\")\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tif n.VectorMatching.FillValues.LHS != nil || n.VectorMatching.FillValues.RHS != nil {\n\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"filling in missing series only allowed between instant vectors\")\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tn.VectorMatching = nil\n\t\tcase n.Op.IsSetOperator(): // Both operands are Vectors.\n\t\t\tif n.VectorMatching.Card == CardOneToMany || n.VectorMatching.Card == CardManyToOne {\n\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"no grouping allowed for %q operation\", n.Op)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tif n.VectorMatching.Card != CardManyToMany {\n\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"set operations must always be many-to-many\")\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tif n.VectorMatching.FillValues.LHS != nil || n.VectorMatching.FillValues.RHS != nil {\n\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"filling in missing series not allowed for set operators\")\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tif (lt == ValueTypeScalar || rt == ValueTypeScalar) && n.Op.IsSetOperator() {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"set operator %q not allowed in binary scalar expression\", n.Op)\n\t\t}\n\n\tcase *Call:\n\t\tnargs := len(n.Func.ArgTypes)\n\t\tif n.Func.Variadic == 0 {\n\t\t\tif nargs != len(n.Args) {\n\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"expected %d argument(s) in call to %q, got %d\", nargs, n.Func.Name, len(n.Args))\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tna := nargs - 1\n\t\t\tif na > len(n.Args) {\n\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"expected at least %d argument(s) in call to %q, got %d\", na, n.Func.Name, len(n.Args))\n\t\t\t} else if nargsmax := na + n.Func.Variadic; n.Func.Variadic > 0 && nargsmax < len(n.Args) {\n\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"expected at most %d argument(s) in call to %q, got %d\", nargsmax, n.Func.Name, len(n.Args))\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tif n.Func.Name == \"info\" && len(n.Args) > 1 {\n\t\t\t// Check the type is correct first\n\t\t\tif n.Args[1].Type() != ValueTypeVector {\n\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(node.PositionRange(), \"expected type %s in %s, got %s\", DocumentedType(ValueTypeVector), fmt.Sprintf(\"call to function %q\", n.Func.Name), DocumentedType(n.Args[1].Type()))\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t// Check the vector selector in the input doesn't contain a metric name\n\t\t\tif vs, ok := n.Args[1].(*VectorSelector); ok && vs.Name != \"\" {\n\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.Args[1].PositionRange(), \"expected label selectors only, got vector selector instead\")\n\t\t\t} else if ok {\n\t\t\t\t// Set Vector Selector flag to bypass empty matcher check\n\t\t\t\tvs.BypassEmptyMatcherCheck = true\n\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.Args[1].PositionRange(), \"expected label selectors only\")\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tfor i, arg := range n.Args {\n\t\t\tif i >= len(n.Func.ArgTypes) {\n\t\t\t\tif n.Func.Variadic == 0 {\n\t\t\t\t\t// This is not a vararg function so we should not check the\n\t\t\t\t\t// type of the extra arguments.\n\t\t\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\ti = len(n.Func.ArgTypes) - 1\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tif t := p.checkAST(arg); t != n.Func.ArgTypes[i] {\n\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(arg.PositionRange(), \"expected type %s in call to function %q, got %s\", DocumentedType(n.Func.ArgTypes[i]), n.Func.Name, DocumentedType(t))\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\tcase *ParenExpr:\n\t\tp.checkAST(n.Expr)\n\n\tcase *UnaryExpr:\n\t\tif n.Op != ADD && n.Op != SUB {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"only + and - operators allowed for unary expressions\")\n\t\t}\n\t\tif t := p.checkAST(n.Expr); t != ValueTypeScalar && t != ValueTypeVector {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"unary expression only allowed on expressions of type scalar or instant vector, got %q\", DocumentedType(t))\n\t\t}\n\n\tcase *SubqueryExpr:\n\t\tty := p.checkAST(n.Expr)\n\t\tif ty != ValueTypeVector {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"subquery is only allowed on instant vector, got %s instead\", ty)\n\t\t}\n\tcase *MatrixSelector:\n\t\tp.checkAST(n.VectorSelector)\n\n\tcase *VectorSelector:\n\t\tif n.Name != \"\" {\n\t\t\t// In this case the last LabelMatcher is checking for the metric name\n\t\t\t// set outside the braces. This checks if the name has already been set\n\t\t\t// previously.\n\t\t\tfor _, m := range n.LabelMatchers[0 : len(n.LabelMatchers)-1] {\n\t\t\t\tif m != nil && m.Name == labels.MetricName {\n\t\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"metric name must not be set twice: %q or %q\", n.Name, m.Value)\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// Skip the check for non-empty matchers because an explicit\n\t\t\t// metric name is a non-empty matcher.\n\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t}\n\t\tif !n.BypassEmptyMatcherCheck {\n\t\t\t// A Vector selector must contain at least one non-empty matcher to prevent\n\t\t\t// implicit selection of all metrics (e.g. by a typo).\n\t\t\tnotEmpty := false\n\t\t\tfor _, lm := range n.LabelMatchers {\n\t\t\t\tif lm != nil && !lm.Matches(\"\") {\n\t\t\t\t\tnotEmpty = true\n\t\t\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tif !notEmpty {\n\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"vector selector must contain at least one non-empty matcher\")\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\tcase *NumberLiteral, *StringLiteral:\n\t\t// Nothing to do for terminals.\n\n\tdefault:\n\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"unknown node type: %T\", node)\n\t}\n\treturn typ\n}\n\nfunc (p *parser) unquoteString(s string) string {\n\tunquoted, err := strutil.Unquote(s)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error unquoting string %q: %s\", s, err)\n\t}\n\treturn unquoted\n}\n\nfunc parseDuration(ds string) (time.Duration, error) {\n\tdur, err := model.ParseDuration(ds)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn 0, The `ParseExpr` method is the main entry point that calls the internal `parseExpr` method, which orchestrates lexing, parsing via the generated YACC parser, and then validation through `checkAST`. The `NewParser` function creates new parser instances with configurable options for experimental features.\\n\\n**Lexer Tokenizer** (promql/parser/lex.go):\\nThe `Lexer` struct implements the tokenization layer, converting input strings into tokens represented as `Item` structs. Each `Item` has a `Typ` (ItemType), position (`Pos`), and value (`Val`). The Lexer uses state functions (`stateFn`) to track parsing state and handle complex constructs like nested parentheses, braces, and brackets. It supports special handling for histogram descriptions and series descriptions used in the testing framework. The `ItemType` enum defines all token types including operators, aggregators, keywords, and special symbols.\\n\\n**AST Node Type Definitions** (promql/parser/ast.go):\\nThe AST is built from several core types: `Node` is the base interface, and `Expr` is the interface for all expressions. It defines token constants for all item types (starting at 57400) and implements the LR parser that constructs the AST based on the grammar rules. The `Functions` map contains all built-in PromQL functions with their type signatures. The promql/functions.go file contains the actual implementation of these functions through the `FunctionCall` type, which is the execution handler for function calls during query evaluation.\\n\\n**Value Type System** (promql/parser/value.go and promql/value.go):\\nThe `ValueType` is a string type defining the PromQL value types: `ValueTypeVector` (instant vector), `ValueTypeMatrix` (range vector), `ValueTypeScalar` (scalar number), and `ValueTypeString`. The `Query` interface represents a prepared query that can be executed with `Exec`. The Engine coordinates with the Parser to parse query strings, then executes the resulting AST against the storage backend. It manages query lifecycle, timeouts, resource limits, and concurrent execution.\\n\\n**Supporting Utilities**:\\n- `promql/parser/posrange/posrange.go`: The `PositionRange` struct tracks error locations in query strings for diagnostic messages\\n- `promql/parser/printer.go` and `prettier.go`: Format AST nodes back to query strings\\n- `promql/parser/features.go`: Manages feature flags for experimental functions\\n- `promql/parser/ast.go`: Additional utilities including `Walk` for traversing the AST, `Inspect` for filtered traversal, and `Visitor` pattern implementation\\n\\n**Data Flow**:\\n1. User provides a query string to `NewParser().ParseExpr()`\\n2. The Lexer tokenizes the input\\n3. The generated YACC parser builds the AST based on the grammar\\n4. The `checkAST` method performs semantic validation and type checking\\n5. The resulting Expr is returned to the Engine\\n6.
